| With the exception of the CIS – an intergovernmental organization and legal successor to the union itself – only states that are former Soviet republics, now members of the United Nations, are listed as successors. |

The **Union of Soviet Socialist Republics**[[t]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-24) (**USSR**),[[u]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-25) commonly known as the **Soviet Union**,[[v]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-26) was a [transcontinental country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_former_transcontinental_countries#Since_1700 "List of former transcontinental countries") that spanned much of [Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia") from 1922 until [it dissolved](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") in 1991. During its existence, it was the [largest country by area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area"), extending across [eleven time zones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_in_Russia "Time in Russia") and sharing [borders with twelve countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_the_Soviet_Union#Borders_and_neighbors "Geography of the Soviet Union"), and the [third-most populous country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population").[[w]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-27) An overall successor to the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire"), it was nominally organized as a [federal union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_union "Federal union") of [national republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union "Republics of the Soviet Union"), the largest and most populous of which was the [Russian SFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_SFSR "Russian SFSR").[[x]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-28) In practice, [its government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_the_Soviet_Union "Government of the Soviet Union") and [economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union "Economy of the Soviet Union") were [highly centralized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet-type_economic_planning "Soviet-type economic planning"). As a [one-party state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-party_state "One-party state") governed by the [Communist Party of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union") (CPSU), it was the flagship [communist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_state "Communist state"). Its capital and largest city was [Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow "Moscow").

The Soviet Union's roots lay in the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution") of 1917. The new government, led by [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin"), established the Russian SFSR, the world's first constitutionally [communist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_state "Communist state"). The revolution was not accepted by all within the [Russian Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Republic "Russian Republic"), resulting in the [Russian Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War"). The Russian SFSR and its subordinate republics were [merged into the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Creation_of_the_Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics "Treaty on the Creation of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics") in 1922. Following [Lenin's death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin%27s_death "Lenin's death") in 1924, [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") came to power, inaugurating [rapid industrialization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Industrialization in the Soviet Union") and [forced collectivization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Collectivization in the Soviet Union") that led to significant economic growth but contributed to a [famine between 1930 and 1933](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1930%E2%80%931933 "Soviet famine of 1930–1933") that killed millions. The [Soviet forced labour camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forced_labor_in_the_Soviet_Union "Forced labor in the Soviet Union") system of the [Gulag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag") was expanded. During the late 1930s, Stalin's government conducted the [Great Purge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge") to remove opponents, resulting in large scale deportations, arrests, and show trials accompanied by public fear. Having failed to build an anti-Nazi coalition in Europe, the Soviet Union signed [a non-aggression pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact") with [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") in 1939. Despite this, in 1941 Germany [invaded the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invaded_the_Soviet_Union "Invaded the Soviet Union") in the largest land invasion in history, opening the [Eastern Front of World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_of_World_War_II "Eastern Front of World War II"). The Soviets played a decisive role in defeating the [Axis powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_powers "Axis powers") while liberating much of [Central and Eastern Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe "Central and Eastern Europe"). However they would suffer an estimated [27 million casualties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union"), which accounted for most losses among the victorious [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II"). In the [aftermath of the war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II"), the Soviet Union consolidated the territory occupied by the [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army"), forming [satellite states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_satellite_states "Soviet satellite states"), and undertook rapid economic development which cemented its status as a [superpower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower "Superpower").

Geopolitical tensions with the United States led to the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"). The American-led [Western Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Bloc "Western Bloc") coalesced into [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") in 1949, prompting the Soviet Union to form its own military alliance, the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact"), in 1955. Neither side engaged in direct military confrontation, and instead fought [on an ideological basis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_imperialism "Cultural imperialism") and through [proxy wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war"). In 1953, following [Stalin's death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalin%27s_death "Stalin's death"), the Soviet Union undertook a campaign of [de-Stalinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De-Stalinization "De-Stalinization") under [Nikita Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev"), which saw reversals and rejections of Stalinist policies. This campaign caused ideological tensions with the [PRC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PRC "PRC") led by [Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong"), culminating in the acrimonious [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split"). During the 1950s, the Soviet Union expanded [its efforts in space exploration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_space_program "Soviet space program") and took a lead in the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race") with the [first artificial satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_artificial_satellite "First artificial satellite"), the [first human spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_human_spaceflight "First human spaceflight"), the [first space station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salyut_1 "Salyut 1"), and the [first probe to land on another planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera_7 "Venera 7"). In 1985, the last Soviet leader, [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev"), sought to reform the country through his policies of _[glasnost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glasnost "Glasnost")_ and _[perestroika](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perestroika "Perestroika")_. In 1989, various countries of the Warsaw Pact [overthrew their Soviet-backed regimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989"), leading to the fall of the Eastern Bloc. A major wave of [nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist "Nationalist") and [separatist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separatist "Separatist") movements erupted across the Soviet Union, primarily in [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan"), [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_(country) "Georgia (country)") and the [Baltic states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states"). In 1991, amid efforts to [preserve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_Union_referendum "1991 Soviet Union referendum") the country as a [renewed federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Union_Treaty "New Union Treaty"), an attempted [coup against Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_attempt "1991 Soviet coup attempt") by hardline communists prompted the largest republics—Ukraine, Russia, and Belarus—to secede. On 26 December, Gorbachev officially recognized the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union"). [Boris Yeltsin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin "Boris Yeltsin"), the leader of the [Russian SFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic"), oversaw its reconstitution into the [Russian Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Federation "Russian Federation"), which [became](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Succession_of_states#Soviet_Union "Succession of states") the Soviet Union's successor state; all other republics emerged as fully independent [post-Soviet states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-Soviet_states "Post-Soviet states"). The [Commonwealth of Independent States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States "Commonwealth of Independent States") was formed in the aftermath of the disastrous Soviet collapse, although the Baltics would never join.

During its existence, the Soviet Union produced [many significant social and technological achievements and innovations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_Soviet_innovation "Timeline of Soviet innovation"). The USSR was one of the most advanced industrial states during its existence. It [had the world's second-largest economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_past_and_projected_GDP_(nominal) "List of countries by past and projected GDP (nominal)") and largest standing military. An [NPT-designated state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons "Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons"), it wielded the [largest arsenal of nuclear weapons in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Russia and weapons of mass destruction"). As an Allied nation, it was a [founding member](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations "Member states of the United Nations") of the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") as well as one of the [five permanent members](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council") of the [United Nations Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council"). Before its dissolution, the Soviet Union was one of the world's two superpowers through its hegemony in Eastern Europe and Asia, global diplomacy, ideological influence (particularly in the [Global South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_South "Global South")), military might, economic strengths, and [scientific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_the_Soviet_Union "Science and technology in the Soviet Union") accomplishments.

Etymology
---------

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Lenin_in_1920_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg/250px-Lenin_in_1920_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_in_1920_(3x4_cropped).jpg)

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Leon_Trotsky_1918_%283x4_rotated_cropped%29.jpg/250px-Leon_Trotsky_1918_%283x4_rotated_cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_1918_(3x4_rotated_cropped).jpg)

The word _[soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet\_(council) "Soviet (council)")_ is derived from the [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language") word _sovet_ (Russian: совет), meaning 'council', 'assembly', 'advice',[[y]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-29) ultimately deriving from the [proto-Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Slavic "Proto-Slavic") verbal stem of *_vět-iti_ ('to inform'), related to Slavic _věst_ ('news'), English _wise_. The word _sovietnik_ means 'councillor'.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Klein-1920-30) Some organizations in Russian history were called _council_ (Russian: совет). In the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire"), the [State Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Council_(Russian_Empire) "State Council (Russian Empire)"), which functioned from 1810 to 1917, was referred to as a Council of Ministers.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Klein-1920-30)

The soviets as [workers' councils](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_council "Workers' council") first appeared during the [1905 Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution "1905 Russian Revolution").[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPonsService2010763-31)[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMccauley2014487-32) Although they were quickly suppressed by the Imperial army, after the [February Revolution of 1917](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_Revolution_of_1917 "February Revolution of 1917"), workers' and soldiers' soviets emerged throughout the country and shared power with the [Russian Provisional Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government "Russian Provisional Government").[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPonsService2010763-31)[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Dewdney-33) The Bolsheviks, led by [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin"), demanded that all power be transferred to the soviets, and gained support from the workers and soldiers.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-34) After the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution"), in which the [Bolsheviks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolsheviks "Bolsheviks") seized power from the Provisional Government in the name of the soviets,[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Dewdney-33)[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-35) Lenin proclaimed the formation of the [Russian Socialist Federal Soviet Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Socialist_Federal_Soviet_Republic "Russian Socialist Federal Soviet Republic") (RSFSR).[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService200584-36)

During the [Georgian Affair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgian_Affair "Georgian Affair") of 1922, Lenin called for the Russian SFSR and other national soviet republics to form a greater union which he initially named as the Union of Soviet Republics of Europe and Asia (Russian: Союз Советских Республик Европы и Азии, romanized:_Soyuz Sovyetskikh Respublik Evropy i Azii_).[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964608Lewin196950Leggett1981354Volkogonov1994421Service2000452%E2%80%93455White2001175-37)[Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") initially resisted Lenin's proposal but ultimately accepted it, and with Lenin's agreement he changed the name to the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics (USSR), although all republics began as _socialist soviet_ and did not change to the other order until [1936](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936_Soviet_Constitution "1936 Soviet Constitution"). In addition, in the regional languages of several republics, the word _council_ or _conciliar_ in the respective language was only quite late changed to an adaptation of the Russian _soviet_ and never in others, e.g. [Ukrainian SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR "Ukrainian SSR").

СССР (in the Latin alphabet: _SSSR_) is the abbreviation of the Russian-language cognate of USSR, as written in [Cyrillic letters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrillic_letters "Cyrillic letters"). The soviets used this abbreviation so frequently that audiences worldwide became familiar with its meaning. After this, the most common Russian initialization is Союз ССР (transliteration: _Soyuz SSR_) which essentially translates to _Union of SSRs_ in English. In addition, the Russian short form name Советский Союз (transliteration: _Sovyetsky Soyuz_, which literally means _Soviet Union_) is also commonly used, but only in its unabbreviated form. Since the start of the [Great Patriotic War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War "Great Patriotic War") at the latest, abbreviating the Russian name of the Soviet Union as СС has been taboo, the reason being that СС as a Russian Cyrillic abbreviation is associated with the infamous _[Schutzstaffel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schutzstaffel "Schutzstaffel")_ of [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany"), as _SS_ is in English.

In English-language media, the state was referred to as the Soviet Union or the USSR. The Russian SFSR dominated the Soviet Union to such an extent that, for most of the Soviet Union's existence, it was colloquially, but incorrectly, referred to as **Russia**.

History
-------

The history of the Soviet Union began with the ideals of the [Bolshevik Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik_Revolution "Bolshevik Revolution") and ended in dissolution amidst economic collapse and political disintegration. Established in 1922 following the [Russian Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War"), the Soviet Union quickly became a one-party state under the [Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union"). Its early years under [Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin "Lenin") were marked by the implementation of socialist policies and the [New Economic Policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Economic_Policy "New Economic Policy") (NEP), which allowed for market-oriented reforms.

The rise of [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") in the late 1920s ushered in an era of intense centralization and totalitarianism. Stalin's rule was characterized by the forced [collectivization of agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Collectivization in the Soviet Union"), rapid [industrialization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Industrialization in the Soviet Union"), and the [Great Purge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge"), which eliminated perceived enemies of the state. The Soviet Union, one of the [Big Four Allied powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Four_(World_War_II) "Big Four (World War II)")[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Justus-38) alongside the United States, the United Kingdom, and China, played a crucial role in the [Allied victory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") in [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), but at a tremendous human cost, with millions of Soviet citizens perishing in the conflict.

The Soviet Union emerged as one of the world's two superpowers, leading the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") in opposition to the [Western Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Bloc "Western Bloc") during the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"). This period saw the USSR engage in an arms race, the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race"), and [proxy wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_wars "Proxy wars") around the globe. The post-Stalin leadership, particularly under [Nikita Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev"), initiated a [de-Stalinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De-Stalinization "De-Stalinization") process, leading to a period of liberalization and relative openness known as the [Khrushchev Thaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khrushchev_Thaw "Khrushchev Thaw"). However, the subsequent era under [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev"), referred to as the [Era of Stagnation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation "Era of Stagnation"), was marked by economic decline, political corruption, and a rigid [gerontocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerontocracy "Gerontocracy"). Despite efforts to maintain the Soviet Union's superpower status, the economy struggled due to its centralized nature, technological backwardness, and inefficiencies. The vast military expenditures and burdens of maintaining the Eastern Bloc, further strained the Soviet economy.

In the 1980s, [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev")'s policies of [Glasnost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glasnost "Glasnost") (openness) and [Perestroika](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perestroika "Perestroika") (restructuring) aimed to revitalize the Soviet system but instead accelerated its unraveling. Nationalist movements gained momentum across the [Soviet republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_republics "Soviet republics"), and the control of the Communist Party weakened. The failed [coup attempt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_attempt "1991 Soviet coup attempt") in August 1991 against Gorbachev by hardline communists hastened the [end of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/End_of_the_Soviet_Union "End of the Soviet Union"), which formally dissolved on 26 December 1991, ending nearly seven decades of Soviet rule.

Geography
---------

With an area of 22,402,200 square kilometres (8,649,500 sq mi), the Soviet Union was the world's largest country,[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-39) a status that is retained by the [Russian Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Federation "Russian Federation").[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-40) Covering a sixth of Earth's land surface, its size was comparable to that of [North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America "North America").[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-41) Two other successor states, [Kazakhstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan") and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine"), rank among the top 10 countries by land area, and the largest country entirely in Europe, respectively. The [European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe "Europe") portion accounted for a quarter of the country's area and was the cultural and economic center. The eastern part in [Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia "Asia") extended to the [Pacific Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") to the east and [Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Afghanistan "Democratic Republic of Afghanistan") to the south, and, except some areas in [Central Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia"), was much less populous. It spanned over 10,000 kilometres (6,200 mi) east to west across 11 [time zones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_zone "Time zone"), and over 7,200 kilometres (4,500 mi) north to south. It had five climate zones: [tundra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tundra "Tundra"), [taiga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiga "Taiga"), [steppes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steppe "Steppe"), [desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert "Desert") and [mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain "Mountain").

The USSR, like [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia"), had the world's longest [border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Border "Border"), measuring over 60,000 kilometres (37,000 mi), or 1+1⁄2 circumferences of Earth. Two-thirds of it was a [coastline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coast "Coast"). The country bordered [Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Afghanistan "Democratic Republic of Afghanistan"), the [People's Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China_(1976%E2%80%931989) "History of the People's Republic of China (1976–1989)"), [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic"), [Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland "Finland"), [Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic"), [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pahlavi_Iran "Pahlavi Iran"), [Mongolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic "Mongolian People's Republic"), [North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea"), [Norway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norway "Norway"), [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic "Polish People's Republic"), [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania "Socialist Republic of Romania"), and [Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") from 1945 to 1991. The [Bering Strait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bering_Strait "Bering Strait") separated the USSR from the United States, while the [La Pérouse Strait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_P%C3%A9rouse_Strait "La Pérouse Strait") separated it from Japan.

The country's highest mountain was Communism Peak (now [Ismoil Somoni Peak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismoil_Somoni_Peak "Ismoil Somoni Peak")) in [Tajikistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic"), at 7,495 metres (24,590 ft). The USSR also included most of the world's largest lakes; the [Caspian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea "Caspian Sea") (shared with [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran")), and [Lake Baikal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Baikal "Lake Baikal"), the world's largest (by volume) and deepest freshwater lake that is also an internal body of water in Russia.

Government and politics
-----------------------

The Soviet [communist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_state "Communist state") system was based on [unified state power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_state_power "Unified state power") and [democratic centralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_centralism "Democratic centralism"). The [highest organ of state authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highest_organ_of_state_authority "Highest organ of state authority"), the [Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_Soviet_Union "Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union"), stood above all other state organs and worked under the leadership of the [Communist Party of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union"). The executive organ of the state (synonymous with government), the [Council of Ministers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_the_Soviet_Union "Council of Ministers of the Soviet Union"), was an internal organ of the All-Union Supreme Soviet.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Sakwa-42)

### Communist Party

[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Moskau_Roter_Platz_September_1964.jpg/250px-Moskau_Roter_Platz_September_1964.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Moskau_Roter_Platz_September_1964.jpg)

Military parade on the [Red Square](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Square "Red Square") in Moscow, 7 November 1964

At the top of the Communist Party was the [Central Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), elected at [Party Congresses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") and Conferences. In turn, the Central Committee voted for a [Politburo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") (called the Presidium between 1952 and 1966), [Secretariat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Secretariat of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") and the [general secretary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") (First Secretary from 1953 to 1966), the _de facto_ highest office in the Soviet Union.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-43) Depending on the degree of power consolidation, it was either the Politburo as a collective body or the General Secretary, who always was one of the Politburo members, that effectively led the party and the country[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-44) (except for the period of the highly personalized authority of Stalin, exercised directly through his position in the Council of Ministers rather than the Politburo after 1941).[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-45) They were not controlled by the general party membership, as the key principle of the party organization was [democratic centralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_centralism "Democratic centralism"), demanding strict subordination to higher bodies, and elections went uncontested, endorsing the candidates proposed from above.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-46)

The Communist Party maintained its dominance over the state mainly through its control over the [system of appointments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nomenklatura "Nomenklatura"). All senior government officials and most deputies of the Supreme Soviet were members of the CPSU. Of the party heads themselves, Stalin (1941–1953) and Khrushchev (1958–1964) were Premiers. Upon the forced retirement of Khrushchev, the party leader was prohibited from this kind of double membership,[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-47) but the later General Secretaries for at least some part of their tenure occupied the mostly ceremonial position of [Chairman of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Presidium_of_the_Supreme_Soviet "Chairman of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet"), the nominal [head of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_the_Soviet_Union "List of heads of state of the Soviet Union"). The institutions at lower levels were overseen and at times supplanted by [primary party organizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kraikom "Kraikom").[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-48)

However, in practice the degree of control the party was able to exercise over the [state bureaucracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Bureaucracy "Soviet Bureaucracy"), particularly after the death of Stalin, was far from total, with the bureaucracy pursuing different interests that were at times in conflict with the party,[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-49) nor was the party itself monolithic from top to bottom, although [factions were officially banned](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ban_on_factions_in_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Ban on factions in the Communist Party of the Soviet Union").[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-50)

### Highest organ of state authority

[![Image 37](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Supreme_Soviet_1982.jpg/250px-Supreme_Soviet_1982.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Supreme_Soviet_1982.jpg)

The [Grand Kremlin Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Kremlin_Palace "Grand Kremlin Palace"), the seat of the [Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_Soviet_Union "Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union"), 1982

The Supreme Soviet (successor of the [Congress of Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Soviets_of_the_Soviet_Union "Congress of Soviets of the Soviet Union")) was nominally the [highest organ of state authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highest_organ_of_state_authority "Highest organ of state authority") for most of the Soviet history,[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-51) at first acting as a rubber stamp institution, approving and implementing all decisions made by the party. However, its powers and functions were extended in the late 1950s, 1960s, and 1970s, including the creation of new state commissions and committees. It gained additional powers relating to the approval of the [Five-Year Plans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Five-year_plans_for_the_national_economy_of_the_Soviet_Union "Five-year plans for the national economy of the Soviet Union") and the [government budget](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_budget "Government budget").[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-52) The Supreme Soviet elected a [Presidium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidium_of_the_Supreme_Soviet "Presidium of the Supreme Soviet") (successor of the [Central Executive Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Executive_Committee_of_the_Soviet_Union "Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union")) to wield its power between plenary sessions,[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Benson,_Shirley-2001-53) ordinarily held twice a year, and appointed the [Supreme Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Soviet_Union "Supreme Court of the Soviet Union"),[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-54) the [Procurator General](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procurator_General_of_the_Soviet_Union "Procurator General of the Soviet Union")[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-55) and the [Council of Ministers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_the_Soviet_Union "Council of Ministers of the Soviet Union") (known before 1946 as the [Council of People's Commissars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_People%27s_Commissars_of_the_Soviet_Union "Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union")), headed by the [Chairman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union "Premier of the Soviet Union") (Premier) and managing an enormous bureaucracy responsible for the administration of the economy and society.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Benson,_Shirley-2001-53) State and party structures of the [constituent republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union "Republics of the Soviet Union") largely emulated the structure of the central institutions, although the Russian SFSR, unlike the other constituent republics, for most of its history had no republican branch of the CPSU, being ruled directly by the union-wide party until 1990. Local authorities were organized likewise into [party committees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raikom "Raikom"), [local Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_(council) "Soviet (council)") and [executive committees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_committee "Executive committee"). While the state system was nominally federal, the party was unitary.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-56)

The state security police (the [KGB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KGB "KGB") and [its predecessor agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:Chronology_of_Soviet_secret_police_agencies "Template:Chronology of Soviet secret police agencies")) played an important role in Soviet politics. It was instrumental in the [Red Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Terror "Red Terror") and [Great Purge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge"),[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-57) but was brought under strict party control after Stalin's death. Under [Yuri Andropov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Andropov "Yuri Andropov"), the KGB engaged in the suppression of political dissent and maintained an extensive network of informers, reasserting itself as a political actor to some extent independent of the party-state structure,[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-58) culminating in the anti-corruption campaign targeting high-ranking party officials in the late 1970s and early 1980s.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-59)

### Unified power and reform

[![Image 38](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/RIAN_archive_699872_Dushanbe_riots%2C_February_1990.jpg/250px-RIAN_archive_699872_Dushanbe_riots%2C_February_1990.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_699872_Dushanbe_riots,_February_1990.jpg)

Nationalist anti-government [riots in Dushanbe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_Dushanbe_riots "1990 Dushanbe riots"), [Tajikistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic"), 1990

The [constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Constitution of the Soviet Union"), which was promulgated in [1924](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1924_Soviet_Constitution "1924 Soviet Constitution"), [1936](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936_Soviet_Constitution "1936 Soviet Constitution") and [1977](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Soviet_Constitution "1977 Soviet Constitution"), did not limit state power.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-60) No [separation of powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers "Separation of powers") existed in the Soviet Union, as the state system was based on the [unified state power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_power "Unified power") of the [highest organ of state authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_state_organ_of_power "Supreme state organ of power"), that is, the [All-Union Supreme Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_Soviet_Union "Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union") which worked under the party's leadership.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-61) The system was governed less by statute than by informal conventions, and no settled mechanism of leadership succession existed. Bitter and at times deadly power struggles took place in the Politburo after the deaths of Lenin[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-62) and Stalin,[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-63) as well as after Khrushchev's dismissal,[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-64) itself due to a decision by both the Politburo and the Central Committee.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Khrushchev,_Nikita-2007-65) All leaders of the Communist Party before Gorbachev died in office, except [Georgy Malenkov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgy_Malenkov "Georgy Malenkov")[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-66) and Khrushchev, who were both dismissed from the party leadership amid internal struggle within the party.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Khrushchev,_Nikita-2007-65)

Between 1988 and 1990, facing considerable opposition, [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev") enacted reforms shifting power away from the highest bodies of the party and making the Supreme Soviet less dependent on them. The [Congress of People's Deputies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_People%27s_Deputies_of_the_Soviet_Union "Congress of People's Deputies of the Soviet Union") was established, the majority of whose members were directly elected in competitive elections held in March 1989, the first in Soviet history. The Congress now elected the Supreme Soviet, which became a full-time parliament, and much stronger than before. For the first time since the 1920s, it refused to rubber stamp proposals from the party and Council of Ministers.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-67) In 1990, Gorbachev introduced and assumed the position of the [President of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_Soviet_Union "President of the Soviet Union"), concentrated power in his executive office, independent of the party, and subordinated the government,[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-68) now renamed the [Cabinet of Ministers of the USSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Ministers_of_the_USSR "Cabinet of Ministers of the USSR"), to himself.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-69)

Tensions grew between the Union-wide authorities under Gorbachev, reformists led in Russia by [Boris Yeltsin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin "Boris Yeltsin") and controlling the newly elected [Supreme Soviet of the Russian SFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_Russian_SFSR "Supreme Soviet of the Russian SFSR"), and communist hardliners. On 19–21 August 1991, a group of hardliners staged a [coup attempt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_attempt "1991 Soviet coup attempt"). The coup failed, and the [State Council of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Council_of_the_Soviet_Union "State Council of the Soviet Union") became the highest organ of state power 'in the period of transition'.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-70) Gorbachev resigned as General Secretary, only remaining President for the final months of the existence of the USSR.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-71)

### Judicial system

The judiciary was not independent of the other branches of government. The Supreme Court supervised the lower courts ([People's Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Court_(Soviet_Union) "People's Court (Soviet Union)")) and applied the law as established by the constitution or as interpreted by the Supreme Soviet. The Constitutional Oversight Committee reviewed the constitutionality of laws and acts. The Soviet Union used the [inquisitorial system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inquisitorial_system "Inquisitorial system") of [Roman law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_law "Roman law"), where the judge, [procurator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procurator_General_of_the_Soviet_Union "Procurator General of the Soviet Union"), and defence attorney collaborate to "establish the truth".[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-72)

### Human rights

[Human rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights "Human rights") in the Soviet Union were severely limited. The Soviet Union was a [totalitarian state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian_state "Totalitarian state") from [1927 until 1953](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1927%E2%80%9353) "History of the Soviet Union (1927–53)")[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-73)[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-74)[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-75)[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-76) and a [one-party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-party "One-party") state until 1990.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-77)[Freedom of speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech") was suppressed and dissent was punished. Independent political activities were not tolerated, whether these involved participation in free [labour unions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_union "Labour union"), private [corporations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corporation "Corporation"), independent churches or opposition [political parties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_parties "Political parties"). The [freedom of movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_movement "Freedom of movement") within and especially outside the country was limited. The state restricted rights of citizens to [private property](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_property "Private property").

According to the [Universal Declaration of Human Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights "Universal Declaration of Human Rights"), [human rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights "Human rights") are the "basic [rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rights "Rights") and [freedoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_(political) "Freedom (political)") to which all humans are entitled."[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-78) including the right to [life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life "Life") and [liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty "Liberty"), [freedom of expression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech"), and [equality before the law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equality_before_the_law "Equality before the law"); and social, cultural and economic rights, including the right to participate in [culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture "Culture"), the [right to food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_to_food "Right to food"), the [right to work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_to_work "Right to work"), and the right to [education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education "Education").

The Soviet conception of human rights was very different from [international law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_human_rights_law "International human rights law"). According to [Soviet legal theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_the_Soviet_Union "Law of the Soviet Union"), "it is the government who is the beneficiary of human rights which are to be asserted _against_ the individual".[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-79) The [Soviet state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_state "Soviet state") was considered as the source of human rights.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_shiman-80) Therefore, the Soviet legal system considered [law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law "Law") an arm of politics and it also considered courts agencies of the government.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes-81) Extensive [extrajudicial powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extrajudicial_punishment "Extrajudicial punishment") were given to the [Soviet secret police agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chronology_of_Soviet_secret_police_agencies "Chronology of Soviet secret police agencies"). In practice, the Soviet government significantly curbed the [rule of law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_law "Rule of law"), [civil liberties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_liberties "Civil liberties"), [protection of law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_justice "Criminal justice") and [guarantees of property](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Property_rights "Property rights"),[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes2001-82)[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes1994-83) which were considered as examples of "bourgeois morality" by Soviet law theorists such as [Andrey Vyshinsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrey_Vyshinsky "Andrey Vyshinsky").[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Vyshinsky1949-84)

The USSR and other countries in the [Soviet Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") had abstained from affirming the [Universal Declaration of Human Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights "Universal Declaration of Human Rights") (1948), saying that it was "overly juridical" and potentially infringed on national sovereignty.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-85): 167–169  The Soviet Union later signed legally-binding human rights documents, such as the [International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Civil_and_Political_Rights "International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights") in 1973 (and the 1966 [International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Rights "International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights")), but they were neither widely known or accessible to people living under Communist rule, nor were they taken seriously by the Communist authorities.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_thomas-hrideas-86): 117  Under [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), the [death penalty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_penalty "Death penalty") was extended to adolescents as young as 12 years old in 1935.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-87)[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-88)[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-89)

[Sergei Kovalev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergei_Kovalev "Sergei Kovalev") recalled "the famous article 125 of the Constitution which enumerated all basic civil and political rights" in the Soviet Union. But when he and other prisoners attempted to use this as a legal basis for their abuse complaints, their prosecutor's argument was that "the Constitution was written not for you, but for American Negroes, so that they know how happy the lives of Soviet citizens are".[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-90)

Crime was determined not as the infraction of law, instead, it was determined as any action which could threaten the Soviet state and society. For example, [a desire to make a profit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speculation "Speculation") could be interpreted as a [counter-revolutionary activity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-revolutionary "Counter-revolutionary") punishable by death.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes-81)[The liquidation and deportation of millions of peasants in 1928–31](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dekulakization "Dekulakization") was carried out within the terms of the Soviet Civil Code.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes-81) Some Soviet legal scholars even said that "criminal repression" may be applied in the absence of guilt.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes-81)[Martin Latsis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Latsis "Martin Latsis"), chief of [Soviet Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Ukraine "Soviet Ukraine")'s [secret police](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheka "Cheka") explained: "Do not look in the file of incriminating evidence to see whether or not the accused rose up against the Soviets with arms or words. Ask him instead to which [class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_class "Social class") he belongs, what is his background, his [education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education "Education"), his [profession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Profession "Profession"). These are the questions that will determine the fate of the accused. That is the meaning and essence of the [Red Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Terror "Red Terror")."[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_State-91)

The purpose of [public trials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Show_trial "Show trial") was "not to demonstrate the existence or absence of a crime – that was predetermined by the appropriate [party authorities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CPSU "CPSU") – but to provide yet another forum for [political agitation and propaganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_propaganda "Soviet propaganda") for the instruction of the citizenry (see [Moscow Trials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_Trials "Moscow Trials") for example). Defense lawyers, who had to be [party members](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CPSU "CPSU"), were required to take their client's guilt for granted..."[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Human_rights_in_the_Soviet_Union_Pipes-81)

### Foreign relations

[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/President_Ford_informally_concludes_the_Vladivostok_Summit_-_NARA_-_7062568.jpg/250px-President_Ford_informally_concludes_the_Vladivostok_Summit_-_NARA_-_7062568.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:President_Ford_informally_concludes_the_Vladivostok_Summit_-_NARA_-_7062568.jpg)

[Gerald Ford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Ford "Gerald Ford"), [Andrei Gromyko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrei_Gromyko "Andrei Gromyko"), [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev") and [Henry Kissinger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Kissinger "Henry Kissinger") speaking informally at the [Vladivostok Summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladivostok_Summit "Vladivostok Summit") in 1974

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/RIAN_archive_330109_Soviet_President_Mikhail_Gorbachev_and_U.S._President_George_Bush.jpg/250px-RIAN_archive_330109_Soviet_President_Mikhail_Gorbachev_and_U.S._President_George_Bush.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_330109_Soviet_President_Mikhail_Gorbachev_and_U.S._President_George_Bush.jpg)

Mikhail Gorbachev and [George H. W. Bush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_H._W._Bush "George H. W. Bush") signing bilateral documents during Gorbachev's official visit to the United States in 1990

During his rule, Stalin always made the final policy decisions. Otherwise, Soviet foreign policy was set by the commission on the Foreign Policy of the Central Committee of the [Communist Party of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), or by the party's highest body the [Politburo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"). Operations were handled by the separate [Ministry of Foreign Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Soviet_Union) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Soviet Union)"). It was known as the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs (or Narkomindel), until 1946. The most influential spokesmen were [Georgy Chicherin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgy_Chicherin "Georgy Chicherin"), [Maxim Litvinov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxim_Litvinov "Maxim Litvinov"), [Vyacheslav Molotov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov "Vyacheslav Molotov"), [Andrey Vyshinsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrey_Vyshinsky "Andrey Vyshinsky"), and [Andrei Gromyko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrei_Gromyko "Andrei Gromyko"). Intellectuals were based in the [Moscow State Institute of International Relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_State_Institute_of_International_Relations "Moscow State Institute of International Relations").[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-92)

*   Comintern (1919–1943), or [Communist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_International "Communist International"), was an international communist organization based in the Kremlin that advocated [world communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_communism "World communism"). The Comintern intended to 'struggle by all available means, including armed force, for the overthrow of the international bourgeoisie and the creation of an international Soviet republic as a transition stage to the complete abolition of the state'.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-93) It was abolished as a conciliatory measure toward Britain and the United States.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-94)
*   [Comecon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comecon "Comecon"), the Council for Mutual Economic Assistance ([Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"): Совет Экономической Взаимопомощи, _Sovet Ekonomicheskoy Vzaimopomoshchi_, СЭВ, _SEV_) was an economic organization from 1949 to 1991 under Soviet control that comprised the countries of the Eastern Bloc along with several communist states elsewhere in the world. Moscow was concerned about the [Marshall Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan"), and Comecon was meant to prevent countries in the Soviets' sphere of influence from moving towards that of the Americans and Southeast Asia. Comecon was the Eastern Bloc's reply to the formation in Western Europe of the Organization for European Economic Co-Operation (OEEC),[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-95)[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-96)
*   The [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact") was a [collective defence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_defence "Collective defence") alliance formed in 1955 among the USSR and its [satellite states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite_state "Satellite state") in Eastern Europe during the Cold War.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Reinalda-2009-97)[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-98) The Warsaw Pact was the military complement to the Comecon, the regional economic organization for the [socialist states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state_(communism) "Socialist state (communism)") of Central and Eastern Europe. The Warsaw Pact was created in reaction to the integration of [West Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany "West Germany") into [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO").[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrump2015-99)[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Reinalda-2009-97) Although nominally a "defensive" alliance, the Pact's primary function was to safeguard the [Soviet Union's hegemony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Empire "Soviet Empire") over its [Eastern European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Bloc "Soviet Bloc") satellites, with the Pact's only direct military actions having been the invasions of its own member states to keep them from breaking away.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-100)[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Reinalda-2009-97)[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrump20151,_17-101)
*   The [Cominform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cominform "Cominform") (1947–1956), informally the Communist Information Bureau and officially the Information Bureau of the Communist and Workers' Parties, was the first official agency of the international Marxist-Leninist movement since the dissolution of the Comintern in 1943. Its role was to coordinate actions between Marxist-Leninist parties under Soviet direction. Stalin used it to order Western European communist parties to abandon their exclusively parliamentarian line and instead concentrate on politically impeding the operations of the [Marshall Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan"), the U.S. program of rebuilding Europe after the war and developing its economy.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-102) It also coordinated international aid to Marxist-Leninist insurgents during the Greek Civil War in 1947–1949.[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-103) It expelled Yugoslavia in 1948 after [Josip Broz Tito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito "Josip Broz Tito") insisted on an independent program. Its newspaper, _For a Lasting Peace, for a People's Democracy!_, promoted Stalin's positions. The Cominform's concentration on Europe meant a deemphasis on world revolution in Soviet foreign policy. By enunciating a uniform ideology, it allowed the constituent parties to focus on personalities rather than issues.[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-104)

#### Early policies (1919–1939)

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/1987_CPA_5896.jpg/250px-1987_CPA_5896.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1987_CPA_5896.jpg)

1987 Soviet stamp

The Marxist-Leninist leadership of the Soviet Union intensely debated foreign policy issues and changed directions several times. Even after Stalin assumed dictatorial control in the late 1920s, there were debates, and he frequently changed positions.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-105)

During the country's early period, it was assumed that Communist revolutions would break out soon in every major industrial country, and it was the Russian responsibility to assist them. The [Comintern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comintern "Comintern") was the weapon of choice. A few revolutions did break out, but they were quickly suppressed (the longest lasting one was in Hungary)—the [Hungarian Soviet Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_Soviet_Republic "Hungarian Soviet Republic")—lasted only from 21 March 1919 to 1 August 1919. The Russian Bolsheviks were in no position to give any help.

By 1921, Lenin, Trotsky, and Stalin realized that capitalism had stabilized itself in Europe and there would not be any widespread revolutions anytime soon. It became the duty of the Russian Bolsheviks to protect what they had in Russia, and avoid military confrontations that might destroy their bridgehead. Russia was now a pariah state, along with Germany. The two came to terms in 1922 with the [Treaty of Rapallo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Rapallo,_1922 "Treaty of Rapallo, 1922") that settled long-standing grievances. At the same time, the two countries secretly set up training programs for the illegal German army and air force operations at hidden camps in the USSR.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-106)

Moscow eventually stopped threatening other states, and instead worked to open peaceful relationships in terms of trade, and diplomatic recognition. The United Kingdom dismissed the warnings of [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") and a few others about a continuing Marxist-Leninist threat, and opened trade relations and _de facto_ diplomatic recognition in 1922. There was hope for a settlement of the pre-war Tsarist debts, but it was repeatedly postponed. Formal recognition came when the new [Labour Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK) "Labour Party (UK)") came to power in 1924.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-107) All the other countries followed suit in opening trade relations. [Henry Ford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Ford "Henry Ford") opened large-scale business relations with the Soviets in the late 1920s, hoping that it would lead to long-term peace. Finally, in 1933, the United States officially recognized the USSR, a decision backed by the public opinion and especially by US business interests that expected an opening of a new profitable market.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-108)

In the late 1920s and early 1930s, Stalin ordered Marxist-Leninist parties across the world to strongly oppose non-Marxist political parties, labour unions or other organizations on the left, which they labelled [social fascists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_fascists "Social fascists"). In the usage of the Soviet Union, and of the Comintern and its affiliated parties in this period, the epithet _[fascist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist\_(insult) "Fascist (insult)")_ was used to describe capitalist society in general and virtually any [anti-Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Soviet "Anti-Soviet") or anti-Stalinist activity or opinion.[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-109) Stalin reversed himself in 1934 with the [Popular Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Front "Popular Front") program that called on all Marxist parties to join with all [anti-Fascist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Fascist "Anti-Fascist") political, labour, and organizational forces that were opposed to [fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism"), especially of the [Nazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi "Nazi") variety.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-110)[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-111)

The rapid growth of power in Nazi Germany encouraged both Paris and Moscow to form a military alliance, and the [Franco-Soviet Treaty of Mutual Assistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franco-Soviet_Treaty_of_Mutual_Assistance "Franco-Soviet Treaty of Mutual Assistance") was signed in May 1935. A firm believer in collective security, Stalin's foreign minister [Maxim Litvinov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxim_Litvinov "Maxim Litvinov") worked very hard to form a closer relationship with France and Britain.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-112)

In 1939, half a year after the [Munich Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich_Agreement "Munich Agreement"), the USSR attempted to form an anti-Nazi alliance with France and Britain.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-113)[Adolf Hitler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler") proposed a better deal, which would give the USSR control over much of Eastern Europe through the [Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact"). In September, Germany invaded Poland, and the USSR also invaded later that month, resulting in the partition of Poland. In response, Britain and France declared war on Germany, marking the beginning of [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II").[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-114)

#### World War II (1939–1945)

Up until his death in 1953, [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") controlled all foreign relations of the Soviet Union during the [interwar period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interwar_period "Interwar period"). Despite the increasing build-up of [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany")'s war machine and the outbreak of the [Second Sino-Japanese War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War"), the Soviet Union did not cooperate with any other nation, choosing to follow its own path.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-115) However, after [Operation Barbarossa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa"), the Soviet Union's priorities changed. Despite previous conflict with the [United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom"), [Vyacheslav Molotov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov "Vyacheslav Molotov") dropped his post war border demands.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-116)

#### Cold War (1945–1991)

The [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War") was a period of [geopolitical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geopolitical "Geopolitical") tension between the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") and the Soviet Union and their respective allies, the [Western Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Bloc "Western Bloc") and the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc"), which began following [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") in 1945. The term _[cold war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold\_war\_(general\_term) "Cold war (general term)")_ is used because there was no large-scale fighting directly between the two [superpowers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpowers "Superpowers"), but they each supported major regional conflicts known as [proxy wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war"). The conflict was based around the ideological and geopolitical struggle for global influence by these two superpowers, following their temporary [alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") and [victory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany "Allied-occupied Germany") against [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") in 1945. Aside from the [nuclear arsenal development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_arms_race "Nuclear arms race") and conventional military deployment, the struggle for dominance was expressed via indirect means such as [psychological warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychological_warfare "Psychological warfare"), propaganda campaigns, [espionage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War_espionage "Cold War espionage"), far-reaching [embargoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_sanctions "Economic sanctions"), rivalry at [sports events](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_and_sports "Politics and sports") and technological competitions such as the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race").

### Administrative divisions

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/%D0%A1%D1%82%D1%80%D1%83%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A0.jpg/250px-%D0%A1%D1%82%D1%80%D1%83%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A0.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%82%D1%80%D1%83%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A0.jpg)

Structure of the Union of SS Republics (1925)

Constitutionally, the USSR was a federation of constituent Union Republics, which were either unitary states, such as [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic") or [Byelorussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic") (SSRs), or federations, such as [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic") or [Transcaucasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcaucasian_Socialist_Federative_Soviet_Republic "Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic") (SFSRs),[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-Sakwa-42) all four being the founding republics who signed the [Treaty on the Creation of the USSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Creation_of_the_USSR "Treaty on the Creation of the USSR") in December 1922. In 1924, during the [national delimitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_delimitation_in_the_Soviet_Union "National delimitation in the Soviet Union") in Central Asia, [Uzbekistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic") and [Turkmenistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmen_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic") were formed from parts of Russia's [Turkestan ASSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkestan_ASSR "Turkestan ASSR") and two Soviet dependencies, the [Khorezm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khorezm_People%27s_Soviet_Republic "Khorezm People's Soviet Republic") and [Bukharan PSPs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bukharan_People%27s_Soviet_Republic "Bukharan People's Soviet Republic"). In 1929, [Tajikistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic") was split off from the Uzbekistan SSR. With the constitution of 1936, the Transcaucasian SFSR was dissolved, resulting in its constituent republics of [Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic"), [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic") and [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic") being elevated to Union Republics, while [Kazakhstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic") and [Kirghizia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kirghiz_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Kirghiz Soviet Socialist Republic") were split off from the Russian SFSR, resulting in the same status.[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-117) In August 1940, [Moldavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic") was formed from parts of Ukraine and [Soviet-occupied Bessarabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_northern_Bukovina "Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and northern Bukovina"), and Ukrainian SSR. [Estonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic"), [Latvia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic") and [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Lithuanian Soviet Socialist Republic") were also [annexed by the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1940) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)") and turned into SSRs, which was [not recognized by most of the international community](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_continuity_of_the_Baltic_states "State continuity of the Baltic states") and was considered an [illegal occupation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states "Occupation of the Baltic states"). After the [Soviet invasion of Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Finland "Soviet invasion of Finland"), the [Karelo-Finnish SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karelo-Finnish_SSR "Karelo-Finnish SSR") was formed on annexed territory as a Union Republic in March 1940 and then incorporated into Russia as the [Karelian ASSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karelian_ASSR "Karelian ASSR") in 1956. Between July 1956 and September 1991, there were 15 union republics (see map below).[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union#cite_note-118)

| 12 | ![Image 57](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Flag_of_the_Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_%281953%E2%80%931991%29%2C_Flag_of_Tajikistan_%281991%E2%80%931992%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_%281953%E2%80%931991%29%2C_Flag_of_Tajikistan_%281991%E2%80%931992%29.svg.png)[Tajik SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic") |
| 13 | ![Image 58](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_the_Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_%281952%E2%80%931990%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_%281952%E2%80%931990%29.svg.png)[Armenian SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic") |
